WELL EVALUATION
Oasis Petroleum North America, LLC
McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T
Figure 1. Precision 96 drilling Oasis Petroleum's McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T well on December
24, 2014 located approximately 9 miles north of Williston in Williams County, North Dakota.
INTRODUCTION
The Oasis Petroleum North America, LLC McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T surface hole location
(NW NW Section 26, T156N, R101W) is located approximately 9 miles north of Williston in Williams
County, ND. The McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T is a horizontal Three Forks first bench well within
the Williston Basin consisting of one 9,644' lateral drilled toward the south. Geologically, the Williston
Basin is an intracratonic, structural, and sedimentary basin located at the western edge of the Canadian
Shield. Within the basin, the Three Forks Formation (Late Devonian) unconformably underlies the
Bakken Formation (Late Devonian ­ Early Mississippian), both of which were deposited during the
Kaskaskia major stratigraphic sequence. The Three Forks consists of mixed carbonates and clastics with
various subdivisions assigned as thorough study of the Three Forks has advanced with the development
of the Bakken `Pool' as an extremely viable oil and gas resource mainly due to the implementation of
hydraulic fracturing technology.
OFFSET WELLS
Offset well data used for depth correlation during curve operations is found under the `Structure' section
appended to this report. The Logan 5601 11-26 8T, located on the same pad as the subject well, was the
primary offset used during the curve landing. Offset well control was essential in curve operations to
successfully land within the Three Forks. Formation thicknesses expressed by gamma ray signatures in
these wells were compared to gamma data collected during drilling operations in order to successfully
land the curve. The target landing true vertical depth (TVD) was updated as necessary to ensure accurate
landing of the curve.
ENGINEERING
The McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T was reentered on November 19, 2014 by Precision 96. Drilling
fluid was diesel-invert mud for the vertical and curve, and brine mud for the lateral. The curve was
landed at 10,910' MD (10,556' TVD) with an inclination of 90.9°.
Following the landing, 7" intermediate casing was set and cemented to 10,862' MD. A 6 PDC bit,
MWD tool, and a 1.5° fixed mud motor were used to drill the lateral. BHA accomplishments are
tabulated in an appendix (BHA Record) to this report. The well reached total depth (TD) at 20,506' MD
at 2355 hrs CST December 24, 2014, generating an exposure of 9,644 linear feet of 6 hole through the
Three Forks interval. The bottom hole location (BHL) lies 10,022.82'south & 566.97' west of surface
location or approximately 315.82' FSL and 22.80' FEL, SE SE Sec. 34, T156N, R101W.
GEOLOGY
Lithology
Sample logging began at 8,040' MD, where the observed lithology consists of primarily siltstone with
thinly interbedded anhydrite and limestone units. The main zones of interest drilled at the subject well
include the Ratcliffe interval and the Mission Canyon, Bakken, and Three Forks formations
The Ratcliffe interval of the Charles Formation (Mississippian - Madison Group) was drilled at 9,004'
TVD (-6,875'), 0' to the Logan 5601 11-26 8T. Samples from the Ratcliffe consist of primarily gray and
off-white dolostone and limestone of similar appearance (Figure 2). Samples have intercrystalline
porosity with trace, light-brown oil staining. Gas shows peaked at 110 units and heavy hydrocarbons
(C1-C2) were observed (for a more detailed hydrocarbon analysis see `Gas and Oil Shows' section
below).
Figure 2. Cuttings of limestone from the
Figure 3. Cuttings of limestone from the
Ratcliffe interval of the Charles Formation.
Mission Canyon Formation.
The Mission Canyon Formation (Mississippian - Madison Group) was drilled at 9,204' TVD (-7,075'),
3' high to the Logan 5601 11-26 8T. Representative samples consist of a gray, off white and brown
laminated to structureless limestone exhibiting intercrystalline porosity and trace, light brown oil stain
(Figure 3). Some samples may contain a trace amount of brown carbonaceous material. Gas shows
peaked at 328 units and heavy hydrocarbons (C1-C2) were observed throughout this interval.
The Middle Bakken member of the Bakken Formation (Late Devonian-Early Mississippian) was drilled
at 10,478' TVD (-8,349'), 2' low to the Logan 5601 11-26 8T. Representative samples consist of a light
gray to light-brown, calcareous silty sandstone with intergranular porosity and a rare, light to
moderate-brown oil stain (Figure 4). Strong hydrocarbon show and heavy gases (C1-C3) were observed
in this interval at a peak of 257 units.
Figure 4. Cuttings of siltstone and dolomitic
Figure 5. Cuttings of dolostone and shale from the first
siltstone from the Middle Bakken interval of the
bench interval of the Three Forks Formation
Bakken Formation.
The first bench interval of the Three Forks Formation (Late Devonian) was drilled at 10,543' TVD
(-8,414'), 3' low to the Logan 5601 11-26 8T. Representative samples consist of a light orange brown,
off white, and light blue gray microsucrosic dolostone with intercrystalline porosity and a rare, spotty
light brown oil stain (Figure 5). Strong hydrocarbon show and heavy gases (C1-C4) were observed in
this interval, peaking at a show of 3,057 units.
Gas and Oil Shows
Hydrocarbon constituents (C1 through C4) are expressed in parts-per-million (ppm) concentrations.
Diesel-invert mud was used to drill the vertical and curve, while brine mud was used to drill the lateral.
During the vertical, gas shows ranged from 55 to 328 units above an average background gas of 40
units. Diesel-invert mud weights in the vertical ranged from 9.7 to 10.15 lb/gal. Ethane (C2) was
observed beginning in the upper Charles Formation and through the end of the vertical.
After kicking off the curve, shows ranged from 110 to 499 units while the background gas averaged near
50 units and the diesel-invert mud had a weight of 10.25-10.35 lb/gal. Shows were markedly higher after
encountering the False Bakken interval of the lower Lodgepole.
During the lateral, shows ranged from 269 to 3,057 units (C1-C4) while the background gas averaged
600 units. Green free oil at the shale-shakers was observed during the lateral portion of the well.
Significantly elevated background gas and increased shows) occurred when the wellbore was near the
interface of the Three Forks first bench and the claystone. Significantly, large intermittent flares (~30'
high) were observed from ~17,100'-17,400' MD when the well bore was 2-4 above the target zone.
GEOSTEERING
The top of the target zone of the McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T is defined by a warm 120-140 api
count marker approximately 1-2 feet into the target zone, while the base of the target zone is marked by
160-180 api count marker indicating the claystone (Figure 6).
Figure 6. Type log showing the gamma signature from the base of the Lower Bakken
Shale to the top of the 1st Claystone. Red lines delineate the Three Forks target zone.
Based on the data obtained from drilling the vertical and curve of the neighboring Logan 5601 11-26 8T,
the curve landing TVD was initially set to be 10,559'. During drilling of the vertical and curve,
formation tops came 3' low to 5' high to the Logan 5601 11-26 8T and the landing target remained
10,559' TVD. The wellbore was landed at a TVD of 10,555.92' at 90.9° inclination about 5' into our
target zone and 5' above Claystone 1.
While drilling the lateral, two distinct gamma markers were primarily used for steering; the warm
(~120-140 API) marker about 1-2' below the top of the target zone, and the hot (~160-180 API) marker
at the base of the target zone indicating the claystone (Figure 7). There were significant difficulties
maintaining the wellbore within our primary target zone, while in zone the BHA bounced erratically.
Above the target zone the BHA built in rotation, and while below our target zone it dropped in rotation.
Similar to the Logan 5601 11-26 8T, there was significant thinning of the zone toward the end of the
lateral by a total of 4', reducing the ta+rget zone from the initial 10' to 6'.

SUMMARY
The Oasis Petroleum North America, LLC McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T was drilled by Precision
96 from reentry to TD in 14 days. The McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T reached a total depth of 20,506'
MD on December 23, 2014. Geologic data, hydrocarbon gas measurements, and sample examination
obtained during the McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T indicate a hydrocarbon rich system in the Three
Forks first bench target. Significant amounts of oil and gas shows were recorded throughout the lateral.
Samples from the target zone consist of light brown, off white, and light pink microsucrosic dolostone
with intercrystalline porosity and a rare, spotty light brown oil stain. Lateral operations were successful
in exposing 9,644' of potentially productive Three Forks first bench rock to the wellbore.
Respectfully submitted,
Christine Maday

LITHOLOGY
McCauley Logan 5601 11-26 6T
Sunburst Geology caught lagged samples in 30' intervals from 8,040' to 20,506' MD (Kibbey-Three Forks 1st
Bench). Formation tops were picked using gamma ray and sample data have been inserted into the sample
descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. The
drilling fluid was diesel invert during the vertical and curve, and brine throughout the lateral.
Vertical Log Descriptions
MD / TVD (MSL Datum)
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation
8,040-8,070
SILTSTONE: red orange, friable, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately cemented, no visible
porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: tan, off white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous, no visible porosity
8,070-8,100
SILTSTONE: red orange, friable, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately cemented, no visible
porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: tan, off white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous, no visible porosity
8,100-8,130
SILTSTONE: as above; SILTY SANDSTONE: cream-off white, light pink, very fine grained, loose-firm,
sub rounded, smooth, moderately sorted, calcareous cement, moderately cemented, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain;
trace ANHYDRITE: tan, off white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous, no visible porosity
Kibbey "Lime"
8,145 MD / 8,144' TVD (-6,015')
8,130-8,160
SILTSTONE: light red orange, pink orange, soft, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately cemented, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain; SILTY SANDSTONE: as above; trace ANHYDRITE: tan, off white, cream, soft,
massive, amorphous, no visible porosity
8,160-8,190
LIMESTONE: mudstone, gray, off white, microcrystalline, soft, crystalline texture, no visible porosity, no
visible oil stain; rare SILTSTONE: light rounded orange, pink orange, soft, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: off white, soft, massive, amorphous, no visible
porosity
8,190-8,220
SILTSTONE: light red orange, rounded brown, soft-firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, gray, off white, microcrystalline, soft-firm,
crystalline texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: off white, soft, massive, amorphous, no
visible porosity
8,220-8,250
SILTSTONE: light red orange, rounded brown, soft-firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, gray, off white, microcrystalline, soft-firm,
crystalline texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: off white, soft, massive, amorphous, no
visible porosity
8,250-8,280
SILTSTONE: light red orange, rounded brown, soft-firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately
cemented, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare LIMESTONE: mudstone, gray, off white, microcrystalline, soft-firm,
crystalline texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: off white, soft, massive, amorphous, no
visible porosity
Charles Salt
8,294' MD / 8,293' TVD (-6,164')

crystalline texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: off white, soft, massive, amorphous, no
visible porosity; trace SALT: translucent, crystalline, hard, subhedral-trace euhedral, crystalline texture

off white, tan, microcrystalline, soft-firm, laminated, crystalline texture, argillaceous in part, no visible porosity, no visible oil
stain

Dear Lauri:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 23797, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be located
approximately down the north-south axis and no closer than 200 feet to the north or south boundaries within
the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 26,27,34 &35 T156N R101W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: OASIS PETROLEUM NORTH AMERICA LLC must ensure the drilling
pit is not constructed in a porous material (i.e.: sand, coal, gravel, or scoria). Effective June 1, 2014, a
covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site
beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back
whenever filtration operations are conducted. OASIS PETRO NO AMER must contact NDIC Field
Inspector Jessica Gilkey at 701-770-7340 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 317'W. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well
head is: 10138'S.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Lauri M. Stanfield

Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the

location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov

RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
